          articles are kept exactly as they appear in the original text; these
          references are crucial for academic integrity and may appear with the
          format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as "[@pmid:33931583;
          @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]", and 4) the revised
          paragraph must encapsulate the entire revision, following the C-C-C
          structure, within a single, cohesive paragraph.

          Context: Understanding how genetic variations influence complex traits

          highlighting disease-relevant gene expression patterns and their

          **Context:** Understanding how genetic variations influence complex
          biological processes and disease-relevant pathways is a fundamental
          goal in the field of genomics and genetics.

          # Revised Paragraph


          ## Context

          Understanding how genetic variations influence complex traits is
          crucial for improving disease treatments. Genes often work together in
          context-specific networks to carry out different functions, and

          Advances in gene expression profiling have provided researchers with a

          Genetic studies have made significant progress in understanding the
          molecular mechanisms underlying complex diseases. One approach, known
          as transcription-wide association study (TWAS), has been particularly
          successful in linking genetic variants to disease risk by examining
          their effects on gene expression.

          provide a mechanistic interpretation for findings from genome-wide
          association studies (GWAS) [@doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1009482;
          @doi:10.1038/ng.3506; @doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1007889;

          scores) [@doi:10.1186/s13059-021-02591-w] and identifying drug
          repurposing opportunities [@doi:10.1038/nn.4618].


          **Conclusion:**

          However, TWAS operates at the individual gene level and may not
          capture the more complex interactions within gene regulatory networks.
          Exploring gene expression patterns and co-expression networks could
          provide a more comprehensive understanding of the biological processes
          underlying complex traits and diseases, potentially leading to the
          identification of novel therapeutic targets and drug mechanisms.

          (GWAS) have become increasingly available, enabling researchers to
          investigate the genetic basis of human diseases. One approach to

              Here is the revised paragraph:


              Given the availability of gene expression data across multiple
              tissues [@doi:10.1038/nbt.3838; @doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03751-6;
              @doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776; @doi:10.1186/s13040-020-00216-9],
              the transcription-wide association study (TWAS) provides an
              effective approach to identify biological processes underlying
              complex traits. TWAS integrates expression quantitative trait loci
              (eQTLs) data to offer a mechanistic interpretation of genome-wide
              association study (GWAS) findings. This approach tests whether
              perturbations in gene regulatory mechanisms mediate the
              association between genetic variants and human diseases
              [@doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1009482; @doi:10.1038/ng.3506;
              @doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1007889; @doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. TWAS has
              been highly successful in understanding disease etiology at the
              transcriptome level [@pmid:33931583;
              @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433], as well as in
              disease-risk prediction (polygenic scores)
              [@doi:10.1186/s13059-021-02591-w] and drug repurposing
              [@doi:10.1038/nn.4618]. However, TWAS operates at the individual
              gene level, which may not capture more complex interactions at the
              network level.


              Key revisions:

              sentence.

              paragraph.

              TWAS in capturing network-level interactions.

              # Revised Paragraph


              **Context:** Advances in genomic technologies have enabled the
              collection of gene expression data across various tissues,
              providing valuable insights into biological processes and disease
              mechanisms.


              **Content:** One effective approach to leverage this data is the
              transcription-wide association study (TWAS), which integrates
              expression quantitative trait loci (eQTLs) to offer a mechanistic
              interpretation of genome-wide association study (GWAS) findings
              [@doi:10.1038/nbt.3838; @doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03751-6;
              @doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776; @doi:10.1186/s13040-020-00216-9].
              TWAS tests whether perturbations in gene regulatory mechanisms
              mediate the association between genetic variants and human
              diseases [@doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1009482; @doi:10.1038/ng.3506;
              @doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1007889; @doi:10.1038/ng.3367], and
              these approaches have been successful in understanding disease
              etiology at the transcriptome level [@pmid:33931583;
              @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433], as well as in
              disease-risk prediction (polygenic scores)
              [@doi:10.1186/s13059-021-02591-w] and drug repurposing
              [@doi:10.1038/nn.4618].


              **Conclusion:** However, TWAS operates at the individual gene
              level, which may not capture the more complex interactions at the

              ## Context

              Advances in gene expression profiling have provided researchers
              with a wealth of data across multiple tissues, enabling new
              approaches to study the biological mechanisms underlying complex
              traits and diseases.


              ## Content

              One such approach is the transcription-wide association study
              (TWAS), which integrates gene expression quantitative trait loci
              (eQTLs) data to provide a mechanistic interpretation of
              genome-wide association study (GWAS) findings. TWAS tests whether
              perturbations in gene regulatory mechanisms mediate the
              association between genetic variants and human diseases
              [@doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1009482; @doi:10.1038/ng.3506;
              @doi:10.1371/journal.pgen.1007889; @doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. This
              approach has been successful in understanding disease etiology at
              the transcriptome level [@pmid:33931583;
              @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433] and has also
              been applied to disease-risk prediction (polygenic scores)
              [@doi:10.1186/s13059-021-02591-w] and drug repurposing
              [@doi:10.1038/nn.4618].


              ## Conclusion

              However, TWAS works at the individual gene level, which may not
              capture the more complex interactions at the network level.

              provide additional insights into disease etiology and potential
              therapeutic targets.

              [@doi:10.1038/nn.4618]. However, TWAS works at the individual gene
              level and may not capture the more complex interactions at the
              network level.


              **Conclusion:** To address this limitation, the present study
              explores the use of gene co-expression patterns to identify
              biological processes and potential therapeutic targets associated
              with complex traits and diseases, thereby providing a more
              comprehensive understanding of disease etiology and drug
              mechanisms.

              trait loci (eQTLs) data to provide a mechanistic interpretation of

              [@doi:10.1038/nbt.3838; @doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03751-6;
              @doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776; @doi:10.1186/s13040-020-00216-9].

              the more complex interactions at the network level. These
              TWAS-based approaches have been highly successful in understanding
